reporter_id IS NOT NULL                                 AND pull_request IS NULL                             GROUP BY gh_user_id, repo_id)                             UNION ALL                             (SELECT cmt_ght_author_id                                AS id,                                     MIN(TO_TIMESTAMP(cmt_author_date, 'YYYY-MM-DD')) AS created_at,                                     repo_id                             FROM commits                             WHERE repo_id = %(repo_id)s                                 AND cmt_ght_author_id IS NOT NULL                                 AND TO_TIMESTAMP(cmt_author_date, 'YYYY-MM-DD') BETWEEN %(begin_date)s AND %(end_date)s                             GROUP BY cmt_ght_author_id, repo_id)                             UNION ALL                            message                             where commits.cmt_id = commit_comment_ref.cmt_id                                 and commits.repo_id = %(repo_id)s                                 and commit_comment_ref.msg_id = message.msg_id                             group by id, commits.repo_id)                             UNION ALL                             (SELECT issue_events.cntrb_id AS id, MIN(issue_events.created_at) AS created_at, issues.repo_id                             FROM issue_events, issues                             WHERE issues.repo_id = 9e7756a0129c73bf773d3c7e2271900456b45b3f work on classes
ae7b7e717fc78de60c288fc4eeb820ca256b7cc8 decided against refactoring out the Augur task collection into its own additional class for a couple reasons. One is I don't want to inherit from the celery classes too much as I feel that is more restrictive on our development, would likely break, and wouldn't really be able to implement a clean encapsulation of functionality in the way that I would want. The last reason is also why I didn't create a seperate class for each element of the AugurTaskRoutine. The main advantage I would see to doing that would to be making assigning dependencies cleaner syntax wise but it would break the rules of encapsulation since I would want it to only allow dependencies between existing task groups as that's the only way it makes sense. I think it makes the most sense to create a class that manages and encapsulates the parts of data collection that the user wants to run along with any dependencies she wants to define.
